## Chapter 6: Concrete Structures




### Introduction

In the previous chapter, we explored the fundamentals of structural analysis and design, focusing on the principles of equilibrium and compatibility. In this chapter, we will delve deeper into the topic of structural analysis, specifically focusing on graphic statics. Graphic statics is a powerful tool used in structural engineering to analyze and design structures. It allows us to visualize and understand the forces and deformations within a structure, providing valuable insights into the structural behavior.

This chapter will cover the basic principles of graphic statics, including the concept of free-body diagrams, the method of joints, and the method of sections. We will also explore the application of these principles in the analysis of statically indeterminate structures. Additionally, we will discuss the importance of understanding the limitations of graphic statics and the need for more advanced methods in certain cases.

The use of graphic statics is not limited to structural engineering. It is also widely used in other fields such as mechanical engineering, civil engineering, and even in the design of machines and mechanisms. Therefore, the knowledge gained from this chapter will not only be beneficial for structural engineers but also for other professionals who deal with structural systems.

In the following sections, we will provide a brief overview of the topics covered in this chapter. We will also provide examples and exercises to help you understand the concepts better. So, let's dive into the world of graphic statics and explore its applications in structural engineering.




### Section: 6.1 Introduction to Graphic Statics:

Graphic statics is a powerful tool used in structural engineering to analyze and design structures. It allows us to visualize and understand the forces and deformations within a structure, providing valuable insights into the structural behavior. In this section, we will provide a brief overview of graphic statics and its applications in structural engineering.

#### 6.1a Basic Concepts

Before delving into the principles of graphic statics, it is important to understand some basic concepts. The first concept is the concept of a structure. A structure is a system of interconnected components that work together to support loads and resist external forces. Structures can be classified into two types: statically determinate and statically indeterminate.

A statically determinate structure is one in which the internal forces and deformations can be determined using the principles of equilibrium and compatibility. This means that the structure has enough degrees of freedom to satisfy the equilibrium equations. On the other hand, a statically indeterminate structure is one in which the internal forces and deformations cannot be determined using the principles of equilibrium and compatibility alone. This is because the structure does not have enough degrees of freedom to satisfy the equilibrium equations.

The second concept is the concept of a free-body diagram. A free-body diagram is a graphical representation of a structure that shows all the external and internal forces acting on it. It is an essential tool in structural analysis as it allows us to visualize the forces and deformations within a structure.

The third concept is the concept of a joint. A joint is a point in a structure where two or more components are connected. It is an important element in structural analysis as it allows us to determine the internal forces and deformations within a structure.

Now that we have a basic understanding of these concepts, let's explore the principles of graphic statics in more detail. In the next section, we will discuss the method of joints, which is a powerful tool for analyzing statically determinate structures.


## Chapter: Building Technologies III: Building Structural Systems II:




### Section: 6.1 Introduction to Graphic Statics:

Graphic statics is a powerful tool used in structural engineering to analyze and design structures. It allows us to visualize and understand the forces and deformations within a structure, providing valuable insights into the structural behavior. In this section, we will provide a brief overview of graphic statics and its applications in structural engineering.

#### 6.1a Basic Concepts

Before delving into the principles of graphic statics, it is important to understand some basic concepts. The first concept is the concept of a structure. A structure is a system of interconnected components that work together to support loads and resist external forces. Structures can be classified into two types: statically determinate and statically indeterminate.

A statically determinate structure is one in which the internal forces and deformations can be determined using the principles of equilibrium and compatibility. This means that the structure has enough degrees of freedom to satisfy the equilibrium equations. On the other hand, a statically indeterminate structure is one in which the internal forces and deformations cannot be determined using the principles of equilibrium and compatibility alone. This is because the structure does not have enough degrees of freedom to satisfy the equilibrium equations.

The second concept is the concept of a free-body diagram. A free-body diagram is a graphical representation of a structure that shows all the external and internal forces acting on it. It is an essential tool in structural analysis as it allows us to visualize the forces and deformations within a structure.

Now that we have a basic understanding of these concepts, let's explore the applications of graphic statics in structural engineering.

#### 6.1b Applications of Graphic Statics

Graphic statics has a wide range of applications in structural engineering. Some of the most common applications include:

- Structural analysis: Graphic statics is used to analyze the structural behavior of buildings, bridges, and other structures. By creating free-body diagrams and using the principles of equilibrium and compatibility, engineers can determine the internal forces and deformations within a structure.

- Design: Graphic statics is also used in the design of structures. By visualizing the forces and deformations within a structure, engineers can make design decisions that ensure the structural stability and safety of the structure.

- Forensic engineering: Graphic statics is used in forensic engineering to investigate structural failures. By analyzing the forces and deformations within a structure, engineers can determine the cause of the failure and make recommendations for future design and construction.

- Education: Graphic statics is an essential tool in the education of structural engineers. By using graphic statics, students can gain a better understanding of the principles of equilibrium and compatibility, and how they apply to real-world structures.

In conclusion, graphic statics is a powerful tool that is widely used in structural engineering. By understanding the basic concepts and applications of graphic statics, engineers can design and analyze structures that are safe, efficient, and sustainable. 


## Chapter 6: Graphic Statics:




### Section: 6.1 Introduction to Graphic Statics:

Graphic statics is a powerful tool used in structural engineering to analyze and design structures. It allows us to visualize and understand the forces and deformations within a structure, providing valuable insights into the structural behavior. In this section, we will provide a brief overview of graphic statics and its applications in structural engineering.

#### 6.1a Basic Concepts

Before delving into the principles of graphic statics, it is important to understand some basic concepts. The first concept is the concept of a structure. A structure is a system of interconnected components that work together to support loads and resist external forces. Structures can be classified into two types: statically determinate and statically indeterminate.

A statically determinate structure is one in which the internal forces and deformations can be determined using the principles of equilibrium and compatibility. This means that the structure has enough degrees of freedom to satisfy the equilibrium equations. On the other hand, a statically indeterminate structure is one in which the internal forces and deformations cannot be determined using the principles of equilibrium and compatibility alone. This is because the structure does not have enough degrees of freedom to satisfy the equilibrium equations.

The second concept is the concept of a free-body diagram. A free-body diagram is a graphical representation of a structure that shows all the external and internal forces acting on it. It is an essential tool in structural analysis as it allows us to visualize the forces and deformations within a structure.

The third concept is the concept of a joint. A joint is a point in a structure where two or more components are connected. It is an important element in structural analysis as it allows us to determine the internal forces and deformations within a structure.

Now that we have a basic understanding of these concepts, let's explore the principles of graphic statics in more detail.

#### 6.1b Principles of Graphic Statics

Graphic statics is based on the principles of equilibrium and compatibility. Equilibrium states that the sum of all forces acting on a body must be equal to zero. Compatibility states that the deformations of a structure must be continuous and compatible with the external loads applied to it.

To apply these principles in graphic statics, we use the method of joints and the method of sections. The method of joints is used to determine the internal forces and deformations at a joint, while the method of sections is used to determine the internal forces and deformations along a section of a structure.

In the method of joints, we analyze the equilibrium of each joint in a structure. This involves summing the forces and deformations acting on each joint and setting them equal to zero. This allows us to determine the internal forces and deformations at each joint.

In the method of sections, we cut a section through a structure and analyze the equilibrium of that section. This involves summing the forces and deformations acting on the section and setting them equal to zero. This allows us to determine the internal forces and deformations along the section.

By combining the method of joints and the method of sections, we can fully analyze and understand the forces and deformations within a structure. This is the basis of graphic statics and is essential in structural engineering.

#### 6.1c Case Studies

To further illustrate the principles of graphic statics, let's look at some case studies. These case studies will provide real-world examples of how graphic statics is used in structural engineering.

##### Case Study 1: Statically Determinate Structure

Consider a simply supported beam with a uniformly distributed load. Using the method of joints, we can determine the internal forces and deformations at each joint. We can also use the method of sections to determine the internal forces and deformations along the beam. By combining these two methods, we can fully analyze the structure and understand its behavior under different loading conditions.

##### Case Study 2: Statically Indeterminate Structure

For a statically indeterminate structure, such as a cantilever beam with a point load at the free end, we cannot use the method of joints alone to determine the internal forces and deformations. In this case, we must use additional methods, such as the slope-deflection method or the moment distribution method, to solve for the unknown internal forces and deformations.

##### Case Study 3: Real-World Application

In a real-world application, graphic statics is used to analyze and design structures such as bridges, buildings, and other civil engineering structures. By understanding the forces and deformations within a structure, engineers can ensure its safety and stability under different loading conditions. Graphic statics is also used in the design of machines and mechanical systems, where understanding the forces and deformations is crucial for their proper functioning.

In conclusion, graphic statics is a powerful tool in structural engineering that allows us to analyze and design structures. By understanding the principles of equilibrium and compatibility and using methods such as the method of joints and the method of sections, we can fully analyze and understand the forces and deformations within a structure. This knowledge is essential for ensuring the safety and stability of structures in our built environment.





### Section: 6.2 Equilibrium Diagrams:

In the previous section, we discussed the concept of a free-body diagram, which is a graphical representation of a structure that shows all the external and internal forces acting on it. In this section, we will focus on a specific type of free-body diagram known as an equilibrium diagram.

#### 6.2a Types of Equilibrium Diagrams

An equilibrium diagram is a type of free-body diagram that shows the forces acting on a structure at a specific point or joint. It is used to determine the equilibrium of a structure, which is the state in which the sum of all forces acting on a structure is equal to zero. This is an important concept in structural analysis as it allows us to ensure that a structure is able to support the loads placed on it without experiencing excessive deformations.

There are two main types of equilibrium diagrams: static and dynamic. A static equilibrium diagram shows the forces acting on a structure at a specific point or joint in a static state, where the structure is not moving. On the other hand, a dynamic equilibrium diagram shows the forces acting on a structure at a specific point or joint in a dynamic state, where the structure is moving.

In this section, we will focus on static equilibrium diagrams. These diagrams are used to determine the equilibrium of a structure in a static state, where the structure is not moving. They are essential in structural analysis as they allow us to determine the internal forces and deformations within a structure.

To create a static equilibrium diagram, we first need to identify the point or joint at which we want to analyze the equilibrium. This point is known as the equilibrium point. Next, we need to draw a free-body diagram of the structure at this point, showing all the external and internal forces acting on it. Finally, we need to apply the principles of equilibrium to the diagram to determine the equilibrium of the structure.

The principles of equilibrium state that the sum of all forces acting on a structure at an equilibrium point must be equal to zero. This means that the sum of all horizontal forces must be equal to zero, and the sum of all vertical forces must also be equal to zero. Additionally, the sum of all moments acting on the structure must also be equal to zero.

By applying these principles to our equilibrium diagram, we can determine the internal forces and deformations within a structure. This information is crucial in structural analysis as it allows us to ensure that a structure is able to support the loads placed on it without experiencing excessive deformations.

In the next section, we will discuss the concept of dynamic equilibrium diagrams and how they are used in structural analysis.





### Section: 6.2 Equilibrium Diagrams:

In the previous section, we discussed the concept of a free-body diagram, which is a graphical representation of a structure that shows all the external and internal forces acting on it. In this section, we will focus on a specific type of free-body diagram known as an equilibrium diagram.

#### 6.2a Types of Equilibrium Diagrams

An equilibrium diagram is a type of free-body diagram that shows the forces acting on a structure at a specific point or joint. It is used to determine the equilibrium of a structure, which is the state in which the sum of all forces acting on a structure is equal to zero. This is an important concept in structural analysis as it allows us to ensure that a structure is able to support the loads placed on it without experiencing excessive deformations.

There are two main types of equilibrium diagrams: static and dynamic. A static equilibrium diagram shows the forces acting on a structure at a specific point or joint in a static state, where the structure is not moving. On the other hand, a dynamic equilibrium diagram shows the forces acting on a structure at a specific point or joint in a dynamic state, where the structure is moving.

In this section, we will focus on static equilibrium diagrams. These diagrams are used to determine the equilibrium of a structure in a static state, where the structure is not moving. They are essential in structural analysis as they allow us to determine the internal forces and deformations within a structure.

To create a static equilibrium diagram, we first need to identify the point or joint at which we want to analyze the equilibrium. This point is known as the equilibrium point. Next, we need to draw a free-body diagram of the structure at this point, showing all the external and internal forces acting on it. Finally, we need to apply the principles of equilibrium to the diagram to determine the equilibrium of the structure.

The principles of equilibrium state that the sum of all forces acting on a structure at a specific point must be equal to zero. This means that the structure is in a state of balance, with no net force acting on it. In other words, the structure is not moving or deforming.

To apply the principles of equilibrium to a static equilibrium diagram, we need to consider the three types of equilibrium: static, dynamic, and thermal. Static equilibrium refers to the state of balance when the structure is not moving. Dynamic equilibrium refers to the state of balance when the structure is moving, but the forces acting on it are balanced. Thermal equilibrium refers to the state of balance when the structure is subjected to thermal loads.

To determine the equilibrium of a structure, we need to consider all three types of equilibrium and ensure that they are satisfied. This means that the sum of all forces acting on the structure at the equilibrium point must be equal to zero for all three types of equilibrium.

In conclusion, equilibrium diagrams are an essential tool in structural analysis. They allow us to determine the equilibrium of a structure in a static state, where the structure is not moving. By applying the principles of equilibrium, we can ensure that a structure is able to support the loads placed on it without experiencing excessive deformations. 





### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the concept of graphic statics and its applications in building structural systems. We have learned about the principles of equilibrium and how to apply them to analyze the stability and strength of structures. We have also discussed the importance of understanding the forces acting on a structure and how to represent them graphically. By using graphic statics, we can gain a deeper understanding of the structural behavior and make informed decisions about the design and construction of buildings.

In this chapter, we will delve deeper into the topic and explore the concept of indeterminate structures. Indeterminate structures are those that cannot be fully analyzed using the principles of statics alone, and require additional methods to determine their behavior. This chapter will cover the various methods used to analyze indeterminate structures, including the slope-deflection method and the moment distribution method. These methods are essential tools for structural engineers and designers, as they allow for a more accurate and efficient analysis of complex structures. We will also discuss the applications of these methods in real-world scenarios, providing a practical understanding of their use. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of indeterminate structures and the methods used to analyze them, equipping them with the knowledge and skills necessary to design and analyze complex structural systems.


## Chapter 7: Indeterminate Structures:




### Subsection: 6.3a Basic Concepts

In the previous chapter, we discussed the principles of equilibrium and how to apply them to analyze the stability and strength of structures. We also learned about the method of joints and the method of sections, which are two commonly used methods for analyzing structures. In this section, we will explore another method for analyzing structures known as the force polygon method.

The force polygon method is a graphical method for analyzing structures that are subjected to multiple forces. It is based on the principle of equilibrium, which states that the sum of all forces acting on a body must be equal to zero for the body to be in equilibrium. This method is particularly useful for analyzing structures that are not statically determinate, meaning that the number of unknowns exceeds the number of equations available for solving.

To apply the force polygon method, we first need to identify all the forces acting on the structure. These forces can be either external forces, such as gravity or wind, or internal forces, such as tension or compression. Once we have identified all the forces, we can represent them graphically as vectors, with the tail of the vector at the point of application and the head of the vector representing the direction and magnitude of the force.

Next, we need to draw a polygon that encloses all the vectors representing the forces. The sides of the polygon represent the resultant forces in each direction. The resultant force is the sum of all the forces acting in that direction. By analyzing the polygon, we can determine the magnitude and direction of the resultant forces and use this information to solve for the unknown forces in the structure.

The force polygon method is a powerful tool for analyzing structures, especially when dealing with indeterminate structures. It allows us to visualize the forces acting on a structure and determine the resultant forces in each direction. By using this method, we can gain a deeper understanding of the structural behavior and make informed decisions about the design and construction of buildings.

In the next section, we will explore the application of the force polygon method in more detail and learn how to use it to analyze different types of structures. 


## Chapter 6: Graphic Statics:




### Subsection: 6.3b Applications of Force Polygon Method

The force polygon method has a wide range of applications in structural engineering. It is particularly useful for analyzing structures that are not statically determinate, meaning that the number of unknowns exceeds the number of equations available for solving. In this subsection, we will explore some of the common applications of the force polygon method.

#### Structural Analysis

The force polygon method is commonly used for structural analysis, where it is used to determine the internal forces and stresses within a structure. By representing the forces acting on a structure as vectors and drawing a force polygon, engineers can visualize the resultant forces and determine the magnitude and direction of the unknown forces. This information is crucial for designing structures that can withstand the expected loads and stresses.

#### Truss Design

Trusses are a common structural element used in buildings and bridges. The force polygon method is particularly useful for analyzing trusses, as it allows engineers to determine the forces acting on each member of the truss. This information is crucial for designing trusses that can support the expected loads and stresses.

#### Stability Analysis

The force polygon method is also used for stability analysis, where it is used to determine the stability of a structure under different loading conditions. By representing the forces acting on a structure as vectors and drawing a force polygon, engineers can determine the resultant forces and determine the stability of the structure. This information is crucial for designing structures that can withstand the expected loads and stresses.

#### Indeterminate Structures

The force polygon method is particularly useful for analyzing indeterminate structures, where the number of unknowns exceeds the number of equations available for solving. By using the force polygon method, engineers can determine the unknown forces and stresses within the structure and use this information to solve for the unknowns. This allows engineers to design structures that can withstand the expected loads and stresses.

In conclusion, the force polygon method is a powerful tool for analyzing structures and is widely used in structural engineering. Its applications range from structural analysis to truss design and stability analysis, making it an essential tool for engineers in the design and construction of safe and efficient structures. 





### Subsection: 6.3c Case Studies

In this subsection, we will explore some real-world case studies where the force polygon method has been applied. These case studies will provide a deeper understanding of the practical applications of the force polygon method and its effectiveness in solving complex structural problems.

#### Case Study 1: Stability Analysis of a Bridge

The force polygon method was used to analyze the stability of a bridge under different loading conditions. The bridge was modeled as a statically indeterminate structure, and the force polygon method was used to determine the unknown forces acting on the bridge. The results of the analysis showed that the bridge was stable under the expected loads, and the design was modified to improve its stability.

#### Case Study 2: Truss Design for a Roof Structure

The force polygon method was used to design the trusses for a roof structure. The trusses were modeled as a statically indeterminate structure, and the force polygon method was used to determine the unknown forces acting on each member of the truss. The results of the analysis were used to design the trusses that could support the expected loads and stresses.

#### Case Study 3: Structural Analysis of a High-Rise Building

The force polygon method was used to analyze the internal forces and stresses within a high-rise building. The building was modeled as a statically indeterminate structure, and the force polygon method was used to determine the unknown forces acting on the building. The results of the analysis were used to design the building that could withstand the expected loads and stresses.

These case studies demonstrate the versatility and effectiveness of the force polygon method in structural engineering. By using this method, engineers can gain a deeper understanding of the forces acting on a structure and use this information to design structures that are safe and efficient. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the concept of graphic statics and its applications in building structural systems. We have learned about the principles of equilibrium and how they can be applied to analyze and design building structures. We have also discussed the different types of forces and moments that act on a structure and how they can be represented using free body diagrams. Additionally, we have delved into the concept of force polygons and how they can be used to determine the resultant force and moment at a point in a structure.

Graphic statics is a powerful tool that can be used to analyze and design building structures. By understanding the principles of equilibrium and how to represent forces and moments using free body diagrams, we can ensure the structural integrity and safety of our buildings. The use of force polygons allows us to simplify complex structural systems and determine the resultant forces and moments at any point.

In conclusion, graphic statics is an essential aspect of building technologies and is crucial for any structural engineer. By mastering the concepts and techniques discussed in this chapter, we can confidently analyze and design building structures that can withstand various loads and forces.

A beam is supported by two pinned supports and a roller support. Draw the free body diagram of the beam and determine the resultant force and moment at the roller support.

## Chapter 6: Graphic Statics:




### Section: 6.4 Funicular Polygon Method:

The Funicular Polygon Method is a graphical technique used in structural engineering to determine the internal forces and deformations in a structure. It is based on the principle of equilibrium and is particularly useful for analyzing structures with multiple supports and varying loads.

#### 6.4a: Introduction to Funicular Polygon Method

The Funicular Polygon Method is a powerful tool for analyzing structures with multiple supports and varying loads. It is based on the principle of equilibrium, which states that the sum of all forces acting on a body must be equal to zero for the body to be in a state of equilibrium. This principle is essential in structural engineering, as it allows engineers to determine the internal forces and deformations in a structure.

The Funicular Polygon Method is a graphical technique that uses a series of lines, called funiculars, to represent the internal forces in a structure. These funiculars are drawn between the supports of the structure and are perpendicular to the direction of the internal forces. The length of the funiculars is proportional to the magnitude of the internal forces, and the direction of the funiculars is determined by the direction of the internal forces.

To use the Funicular Polygon Method, engineers must first determine the external forces acting on the structure. This can be done through a force analysis, which involves breaking down the structure into smaller elements and analyzing the forces acting on each element. Once the external forces are known, engineers can draw the funiculars and determine the internal forces and deformations in the structure.

One of the key advantages of the Funicular Polygon Method is its ability to handle complex structures with multiple supports and varying loads. It allows engineers to easily visualize the internal forces and deformations in a structure, making it a valuable tool for structural analysis.

In the next section, we will explore the applications of the Funicular Polygon Method in more detail and discuss how it can be used to analyze different types of structures.


#### 6.4b: Applications of Funicular Polygon Method

The Funicular Polygon Method has a wide range of applications in structural engineering. It is particularly useful for analyzing structures with multiple supports and varying loads. In this section, we will explore some of the key applications of this method.

##### Structural Analysis

The primary application of the Funicular Polygon Method is in structural analysis. As mentioned earlier, this method is based on the principle of equilibrium, which is essential in determining the internal forces and deformations in a structure. By using the Funicular Polygon Method, engineers can easily visualize the internal forces and deformations in a structure, making it a valuable tool for analyzing the structural integrity of a building.

##### Design of Structures

The Funicular Polygon Method is also useful in the design of structures. By analyzing the internal forces and deformations in a structure, engineers can identify potential weak points and make design modifications to improve the structural stability of a building. This method is particularly useful for designing structures that can withstand varying loads, such as bridges and high-rise buildings.

##### Forensic Engineering

The Funicular Polygon Method has also been used in forensic engineering to investigate structural failures. By analyzing the internal forces and deformations in a structure, engineers can determine the cause of a failure and make recommendations for future design improvements. This method has been used in the investigation of various structural failures, including the collapse of the Hyatt Regency walkway in Kansas City, Missouri, and the collapse of the Tacoma Narrows Bridge in Washington.

##### Educational Tool

The Funicular Polygon Method is also a valuable educational tool for teaching students about structural analysis and design. By using this method, students can gain a better understanding of the principles of equilibrium and how they apply to real-world structures. This method is particularly useful for visual learners, as it allows them to see the internal forces and deformations in a structure, making it easier to understand complex concepts.

In conclusion, the Funicular Polygon Method is a powerful tool for analyzing structures with multiple supports and varying loads. Its applications in structural analysis, design, forensic engineering, and education make it an essential topic for any student studying building technologies. ## Chapter: Building Technologies III: Building Structural Systems II

### Introduction

In the previous chapter, we explored the fundamentals of building structural systems and how they are designed to withstand various forces and loads. In this chapter, we will delve deeper into the topic of structural systems and focus on the concept of indeterminate structures. Indeterminate structures are those that cannot be fully analyzed using the principles of statics alone, and require additional methods to determine their behavior. This chapter will cover the various methods used to analyze indeterminate structures, including the slope-deflection method and the moment distribution method.

The slope-deflection method is a graphical method used to determine the deflections and internal forces in a structure. It is based on the principle of superposition, where the deflections and forces in a structure are calculated by summing the deflections and forces caused by each individual load. This method is particularly useful for analyzing structures with multiple supports and varying loads.

The moment distribution method, on the other hand, is a numerical method used to determine the deflections and internal forces in a structure. It is based on the principle of energy conservation, where the deflections and forces in a structure are calculated by distributing the applied loads along the length of the structure. This method is particularly useful for analyzing structures with multiple supports and varying loads, as it allows for a more accurate determination of the deflections and forces.

In this chapter, we will explore the principles behind these methods and how they are applied to analyze indeterminate structures. We will also discuss the advantages and limitations of each method, and how they can be used in conjunction with other methods to fully analyze a structure. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the slope-deflection and moment distribution methods, and be able to apply them to analyze indeterminate structures in their own designs.


## Chapter 7: Indeterminate Structures:




### Section: 6.4 Funicular Polygon Method:

The Funicular Polygon Method is a powerful tool for analyzing structures with multiple supports and varying loads. It is based on the principle of equilibrium, which states that the sum of all forces acting on a body must be equal to zero for the body to be in a state of equilibrium. This principle is essential in structural engineering, as it allows engineers to determine the internal forces and deformations in a structure.

#### 6.4a: Introduction to Funicular Polygon Method

The Funicular Polygon Method is a graphical technique that uses a series of lines, called funiculars, to represent the internal forces in a structure. These funiculars are drawn between the supports of the structure and are perpendicular to the direction of the internal forces. The length of the funiculars is proportional to the magnitude of the internal forces, and the direction of the funiculars is determined by the direction of the internal forces.

To use the Funicular Polygon Method, engineers must first determine the external forces acting on the structure. This can be done through a force analysis, which involves breaking down the structure into smaller elements and analyzing the forces acting on each element. Once the external forces are known, engineers can draw the funiculars and determine the internal forces and deformations in the structure.

One of the key advantages of the Funicular Polygon Method is its ability to handle complex structures with multiple supports and varying loads. It allows engineers to easily visualize the internal forces and deformations in a structure, making it a valuable tool for structural analysis.

#### 6.4b: Steps for Using the Funicular Polygon Method

To use the Funicular Polygon Method, engineers must follow these steps:

1. Identify the supports of the structure and draw a polygon around them.
2. Determine the external forces acting on the structure and draw funiculars from each support to the point of application of the external forces.
3. Draw funiculars between the supports that are not connected by external forces.
4. The length of the funiculars is proportional to the magnitude of the internal forces.
5. The direction of the funiculars is determined by the direction of the internal forces.
6. The funiculars must be perpendicular to the direction of the internal forces.
7. The funiculars must form a closed polygon.
8. The internal forces and deformations can be determined by analyzing the funicular polygon.

#### 6.4c: Case Studies

To further illustrate the use of the Funicular Polygon Method, let's look at some case studies.

##### Case Study 1: Truss Structure

Consider a truss structure with three supports and a uniformly distributed load of 10 kN/m on the top chord. The external forces acting on the structure are the reactions at the supports and the distributed load. Using the Funicular Polygon Method, we can determine the internal forces and deformations in the truss.

1. Identify the supports and draw a polygon around them.
2. Determine the external forces acting on the structure and draw funiculars from each support to the point of application of the external forces.
3. Draw funiculars between the supports that are not connected by external forces.
4. The length of the funiculars is proportional to the magnitude of the internal forces.
5. The direction of the funiculars is determined by the direction of the internal forces.
6. The funiculars must be perpendicular to the direction of the internal forces.
7. The funiculars must form a closed polygon.
8. The internal forces and deformations can be determined by analyzing the funicular polygon.

##### Case Study 2: Cantilever Beam

Consider a cantilever beam with a uniformly distributed load of 20 kN/m on the free end. The external forces acting on the structure are the reaction at the fixed support and the distributed load. Using the Funicular Polygon Method, we can determine the internal forces and deformations in the beam.

1. Identify the supports and draw a polygon around them.
2. Determine the external forces acting on the structure and draw funiculars from each support to the point of application of the external forces.
3. Draw funiculars between the supports that are not connected by external forces.
4. The length of the funiculars is proportional to the magnitude of the internal forces.
5. The direction of the funiculars is determined by the direction of the internal forces.
6. The funiculars must be perpendicular to the direction of the internal forces.
7. The funiculars must form a closed polygon.
8. The internal forces and deformations can be determined by analyzing the funicular polygon.

#### 6.4d: Conclusion

The Funicular Polygon Method is a powerful tool for analyzing structures with multiple supports and varying loads. It allows engineers to easily visualize the internal forces and deformations in a structure, making it a valuable tool for structural analysis. By following the steps outlined in this section, engineers can use the Funicular Polygon Method to determine the internal forces and deformations in a structure. 





### Section: 6.5 Graphic Statics Applications:

Graphic statics is a powerful tool for analyzing structures and understanding their behavior under different loading conditions. In this section, we will explore some of the applications of graphic statics in structural design.

#### 6.5a Applications in Structural Design

Graphic statics has a wide range of applications in structural design. It is used to analyze the behavior of structures under different loading conditions, such as gravity, wind, and seismic loads. It is also used to determine the internal forces and deformations in a structure, which are crucial for designing safe and efficient structures.

One of the key applications of graphic statics in structural design is the analysis of truss structures. Trusses are commonly used in building construction, and their behavior under different loading conditions can be complex. Graphic statics allows engineers to easily visualize the internal forces and deformations in a truss, making it a valuable tool for designing and analyzing these structures.

Another important application of graphic statics is in the design of bridges. Bridges are subjected to a variety of loading conditions, and their behavior must be carefully analyzed to ensure their safety and stability. Graphic statics allows engineers to determine the internal forces and deformations in a bridge, which are crucial for designing a structure that can withstand these forces.

Graphic statics is also used in the design of foundations for buildings. Foundations are responsible for supporting the weight of a building, and their behavior under different loading conditions must be carefully analyzed. Graphic statics allows engineers to determine the internal forces and deformations in a foundation, which are crucial for designing a structure that can support the weight of the building.

In addition to these applications, graphic statics is also used in the design of other structural elements, such as beams, columns, and connections. It is a versatile tool that is essential for understanding the behavior of structures and designing safe and efficient structures.

### Subsection: 6.5b Applications in Structural Analysis

Graphic statics is not only useful in structural design, but also in structural analysis. Structural analysis involves studying the behavior of structures under different loading conditions and determining their response to these conditions. Graphic statics allows engineers to easily visualize the internal forces and deformations in a structure, making it a valuable tool for analyzing the behavior of structures.

One of the key applications of graphic statics in structural analysis is the determination of structural stability. Structural stability refers to the ability of a structure to resist external forces and maintain its equilibrium. Graphic statics allows engineers to determine the stability of a structure by analyzing the internal forces and deformations in the structure.

Another important application of graphic statics in structural analysis is the determination of structural strength. Structural strength refers to the ability of a structure to withstand external forces without failing. Graphic statics allows engineers to determine the strength of a structure by analyzing the internal forces and deformations in the structure.

Graphic statics is also used in the analysis of structural vibrations. Structural vibrations can occur due to external forces, such as wind or earthquakes, or internal forces, such as mechanical vibrations. Graphic statics allows engineers to determine the natural frequencies of a structure, which are crucial for designing structures that can withstand these vibrations.

In conclusion, graphic statics has a wide range of applications in structural design and analysis. It is a powerful tool that allows engineers to easily visualize the internal forces and deformations in a structure, making it an essential tool for designing safe and efficient structures. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the concept of graphic statics and its applications in building structural systems. We have learned about the principles of equilibrium and how they can be applied to analyze the stability and strength of structures. We have also discussed the different types of forces and their effects on structures, as well as the importance of considering all external and internal forces when designing a structure.

Graphic statics is a powerful tool that allows us to visualize and analyze the behavior of structures under different loading conditions. By using graphical methods, we can easily determine the equilibrium of a structure and identify potential weak points or areas of concern. This information is crucial in the design and construction of safe and efficient buildings.

As we conclude this chapter, it is important to note that graphic statics is just one of the many tools and techniques used in building structural systems. It is essential for engineers and designers to have a thorough understanding of all aspects of structural analysis and design in order to create safe and reliable structures.

## Chapter 7: Structural Analysis:




### Section: 6.5c Case Studies

In this section, we will explore some real-world case studies where graphic statics has been used to analyze and solve structural problems.

#### 6.5c.1 Collapse of the Hyatt Regency Hotel Walkway

In 1981, the Hyatt Regency Hotel in Kansas City, Missouri, experienced a tragic collapse of a suspended walkway on the fourth floor. The walkway, which was suspended from the ceiling by a series of steel rods, collapsed under the weight of a crowd of people. The collapse resulted in the death of 114 people and injuries to over 200 others.

Graphic statics was used to analyze the structural failure and determine the cause of the collapse. The analysis revealed that the design of the walkway was flawed, with the steel rods being unable to support the weight of the walkway and the crowd. This case study highlights the importance of thorough structural analysis and the potential consequences of design flaws.

#### 6.5c.2 Structural Analysis of the Tacoma Narrows Bridge

The Tacoma Narrows Bridge, also known as the Galloping Gertie, is a suspension bridge in Washington state that experienced severe vibrations and eventual collapse just four months after its opening in 1940. The bridge was designed to be lightweight and flexible, but this flexibility proved to be its downfall as it was unable to withstand the wind forces acting on it.

Graphic statics was used to analyze the structural behavior of the bridge and determine the cause of its collapse. The analysis revealed that the bridge was unable to withstand the wind forces acting on it, leading to severe vibrations and eventual collapse. This case study highlights the importance of considering all loading conditions, including wind forces, in structural analysis.

#### 6.5c.3 Structural Analysis of the World Trade Center Towers

The World Trade Center towers in New York City, which stood at 110 stories tall, were designed to withstand a variety of loading conditions, including wind forces and seismic activity. However, on September 11, 2001, the towers were severely damaged and eventually collapsed due to the impact of two airplanes.

Graphic statics was used to analyze the structural behavior of the towers and determine the cause of their collapse. The analysis revealed that the impact of the airplanes caused significant damage to the structural columns, leading to a domino effect and eventual collapse. This case study highlights the importance of considering extreme loading conditions, such as terrorist attacks, in structural analysis.

### Conclusion

These case studies demonstrate the power and versatility of graphic statics in structural analysis. By using graphical methods to analyze structures, engineers can gain a better understanding of their behavior under different loading conditions and make informed design decisions. As technology continues to advance, graphic statics will play an increasingly important role in the field of structural engineering.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the concept of graphic statics and its applications in building structural systems. We have learned about the principles of equilibrium and how they can be applied to analyze the stability and strength of structures. We have also discussed the different types of forces and moments that act on a structure and how they can be represented graphically. Additionally, we have examined the concept of free-body diagrams and how they can be used to visualize the forces and moments acting on a structure.

Graphic statics is a powerful tool that allows us to analyze and understand the behavior of structures. By using graphical methods, we can easily visualize the forces and moments acting on a structure and determine its stability and strength. This is especially useful in the field of building technology, where structures are constantly subjected to various forces and loads.

In conclusion, graphic statics is an essential tool for any building technology professional. It allows us to analyze and understand the behavior of structures, ensuring their safety and stability. By applying the principles of equilibrium and using graphical methods, we can design and construct structures that can withstand various forces and loads.

### Exercises
#### Exercise 1
Consider a simply supported beam with a uniformly distributed load. Draw the free-body diagram of the beam and determine the reactions at the supports.

#### Exercise 2
A cantilever beam is subjected to a point load at its free end. Draw the free-body diagram of the beam and determine the reactions at the support.

#### Exercise 3
A truss structure is subjected to a vertical load at its center. Draw the free-body diagram of the truss and determine the reactions at the supports.

#### Exercise 4
A frame structure is subjected to a horizontal force at one of its corners. Draw the free-body diagram of the frame and determine the reactions at the supports.

#### Exercise 5
A crane is lifting a load with a cable attached to its boom. Draw the free-body diagram of the crane and determine the tension in the cable.

In the context of building technologies, statics plays a crucial role in the design and analysis of structural systems. It helps engineers and architects understand how forces act on a building and how they can be controlled to ensure the safety and stability of the structure.

The study of statics is essential for anyone involved in the field of building technologies. It provides a fundamental understanding of the forces that act on a building and how they can be managed to ensure the structural integrity of the building. This knowledge is crucial for designing safe and efficient buildings that can withstand various external forces such as gravity, wind, and seismic activity.

In this chapter, we will cover various topics related to statics, including the principles of equilibrium, forces and moments, and structural analysis. We will also discuss the different types of structural systems used in building technologies, such as frame, shell, and membrane structures. Additionally, we will explore the concept of structural stability and how it is affected by external forces.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of statics in building technologies. ### Exercises

A beam is supported by two pins at its ends and is subjected to a uniformly distributed load of 10 kN/m. Determine the reactions at the supports and the maximum bending moment in the beam.

A cantilever beam is subjected to a point load of 20 kN at its free end. Determine the reactions at the support and the maximum deflection of the beam.
