## Chapter 7: Analysis of Building Structural Systems:




### Introduction

Welcome to Chapter 7 of "Building Technologies III: Building Structural Systems II". In this chapter, we will be discussing the building envelope, a crucial component of any structure. The building envelope is the outermost layer of a building that separates the interior from the exterior. It is designed to protect the building and its occupants from external elements such as weather, noise, and pollution.

The building envelope plays a vital role in maintaining the comfort and safety of the building's occupants. It is responsible for regulating the flow of air, light, and heat, and it also provides structural support to the building. The design and construction of the building envelope require careful consideration of various factors, including the building's location, climate, and occupant needs.

In this chapter, we will explore the different types of building envelopes, their components, and their functions. We will also discuss the various materials and techniques used in building envelope construction, as well as the latest advancements in envelope technology. Additionally, we will cover the importance of envelope design in energy efficiency and sustainability, and how it can contribute to the overall performance of a building.

Whether you are a student, a professional, or simply interested in learning more about building technologies, this chapter will provide you with a comprehensive understanding of building envelopes. So let's dive in and explore the fascinating world of building envelopes.




### Section: 7.1 Building Envelope Systems:

The building envelope is a crucial component of any structure, as it serves as the barrier between the interior and exterior of a building. It is responsible for regulating the flow of air, light, and heat, and it also provides structural support to the building. In this section, we will explore the different types of building envelope systems and their components.

#### 7.1a Types of Building Envelope Systems

There are three main types of building envelope systems: curtain wall, structural glazing, and structural silicone glazing. Each type has its own unique characteristics and is used in different types of buildings.

##### Curtain Wall

A curtain wall is a non-load-bearing exterior wall that is used to enclose a building. It is typically made of aluminum or steel frames with glass or other cladding panels. The curtain wall is designed to provide a seamless and weather-tight barrier between the interior and exterior of a building. It is commonly used in high-rise buildings and is known for its strength and durability.

##### Structural Glazing

Structural glazing is a type of building envelope system that uses glass as the primary structural element. It is typically used in buildings with large glass surfaces, such as skyscrapers. Structural glazing is known for its strength and ability to withstand high wind and seismic loads. It is also commonly used in buildings with a modern and minimalist design.

##### Structural Silicone Glazing

Structural silicone glazing is a type of building envelope system that uses silicone as the primary sealant for glazing. It is commonly used in buildings with large glass surfaces, such as curtain walls and structural glazing. Structural silicone glazing is known for its durability and ability to withstand extreme weather conditions. It is also commonly used in buildings with a modern and minimalist design.

### Subsection: 7.1b Building Envelope Components

The building envelope is made up of various components that work together to protect the building and its occupants from external elements. These components include:

#### Exterior Wall

The exterior wall is the outermost layer of the building envelope. It is responsible for providing structural support and protecting the building from external weather conditions. The exterior wall is typically made of brick, stone, or concrete and is designed to withstand high wind and seismic loads.

#### Windows and Doors

Windows and doors are essential components of the building envelope. They allow natural light and ventilation into the building while also providing a means of entry and exit. Windows and doors are typically made of glass and frames, and they are designed to be weather-tight and energy-efficient.

#### Roof

The roof is the uppermost layer of the building envelope. It is responsible for protecting the building from rain, snow, and other weather conditions. The roof is typically made of shingles, tiles, or metal and is designed to withstand high wind and seismic loads.

#### Foundation

The foundation is the lowest layer of the building envelope. It is responsible for providing structural support and protecting the building from external forces such as soil pressure and groundwater. The foundation is typically made of concrete and is designed to be durable and resistant to external forces.

### Subsection: 7.1c Design Considerations for Building Envelope Systems

When designing a building envelope system, there are several important considerations that must be taken into account. These include:

#### Energy Efficiency

The building envelope plays a crucial role in maintaining the energy efficiency of a building. It is important to consider the U-value of the building envelope, which measures its ability to resist heat transfer. The lower the U-value, the more energy-efficient the building envelope is.

#### Durability

The building envelope must be able to withstand extreme weather conditions and maintain its integrity over time. It is important to consider the materials used and their ability to withstand high wind, seismic, and moisture loads.

#### Aesthetics

The building envelope is not only functional but also plays a significant role in the overall design of a building. It is important to consider the aesthetic appeal of the building envelope and how it complements the overall design of the building.

#### Maintenance

The building envelope must be easy to maintain and clean. This is especially important for large buildings with multiple floors, where maintenance can be a challenge. It is important to consider the materials used and their ability to withstand wear and tear.

#### Cost

The cost of the building envelope must be considered, both in terms of initial construction and long-term maintenance. It is important to balance the cost with the desired level of energy efficiency and durability.

In conclusion, the building envelope is a crucial component of any structure, and it is important to carefully consider its design and components. By understanding the different types of building envelope systems and their components, as well as the important design considerations, architects and engineers can create a durable and energy-efficient building envelope that will protect the building and its occupants for years to come.





### Subsection: 7.1b Design of Building Envelope Systems

The design of building envelope systems is a crucial aspect of building construction. It involves the selection and integration of various components to create a functional and efficient barrier between the interior and exterior of a building. In this subsection, we will explore the key considerations and principles in the design of building envelope systems.

#### 7.1b.1 Key Considerations in Building Envelope Design

When designing a building envelope, there are several key considerations that must be taken into account. These include the building's location, climate, and intended use, as well as the building's structural system and budget. The building's location and climate will determine the type of weather conditions the envelope will need to withstand, such as extreme temperatures, precipitation, and wind. The intended use of the building will also impact the design, as certain types of buildings may require more robust envelopes to withstand specific loads. The building's structural system and budget will also play a role in the design, as the envelope must be able to support the structural loads and fit within the overall budget.

#### 7.1b.2 Principles of Building Envelope Design

There are several principles that guide the design of building envelopes. These include durability, energy efficiency, and aesthetics. Durability refers to the ability of the envelope to withstand the expected weather conditions and loads over time. Energy efficiency is also a crucial consideration, as the envelope plays a significant role in regulating the building's energy consumption. The envelope must be designed to minimize heat loss and gain, as well as to control air and moisture infiltration. Aesthetics also play a role in envelope design, as the envelope must complement the overall design of the building and contribute to its visual appeal.

#### 7.1b.3 Design Process for Building Envelope Systems

The design process for building envelope systems typically follows a systematic approach. It begins with a thorough analysis of the building's location, climate, and intended use. This is followed by the selection of appropriate envelope components, such as cladding materials, windows, and insulation. The design must also consider the integration of these components with the building's structural system and budget. Once the design is finalized, it is important to conduct performance analysis and testing to ensure that the envelope meets the desired criteria.

#### 7.1b.4 Future Trends in Building Envelope Design

As technology and sustainability continue to play a significant role in building construction, there are several emerging trends in building envelope design. These include the use of advanced materials, such as smart glass and self-healing concrete, as well as the integration of renewable energy sources, such as solar panels and wind turbines. Additionally, there is a growing focus on biophilic design, which incorporates natural elements and principles into the building's design, including the envelope. As these trends continue to evolve, the design of building envelopes will become even more complex and innovative.





### Section: 7.1c Case Studies

In this section, we will explore some real-world case studies that demonstrate the application of building envelope systems. These case studies will provide a deeper understanding of the principles and considerations discussed in the previous section.

#### 7.1c.1 Case Study 1: The Guggenheim Museum Bilbao

The Guggenheim Museum Bilbao, designed by Frank Gehry, is a prime example of a building with a unique and innovative envelope system. The building's iconic curves and undulating surfaces are achieved through a combination of steel, glass, and titanium panels. The envelope not only provides structural support but also adds to the building's aesthetic appeal. The design team had to consider the building's location in the Basque region of Spain, which experiences strong winds and heavy rainfall. The envelope was designed to withstand these conditions while also allowing natural light to enter the building.

#### 7.1c.2 Case Study 2: The Burj Khalifa

The Burj Khalifa, the tallest building in the world, also has a unique envelope system. The building's skin is made up of a combination of glass and aluminum panels, which were prefabricated and then installed on-site. The envelope not only provides structural support but also helps to regulate the building's energy consumption. The design team had to consider the building's location in the desert climate of Dubai, which experiences extreme temperatures. The envelope was designed to minimize heat gain and loss, as well as to control air and moisture infiltration.

#### 7.1c.3 Case Study 3: The Seattle Central Library

The Seattle Central Library, designed by Rem Koolhaas, is another example of a building with a unique envelope system. The building's skin is made up of a combination of glass, aluminum, and concrete panels. The envelope not only provides structural support but also adds to the building's aesthetic appeal. The design team had to consider the building's location in the Pacific Northwest region of the United States, which experiences mild temperatures and heavy rainfall. The envelope was designed to withstand these conditions while also allowing natural light to enter the building.

### Conclusion

These case studies demonstrate the importance of considering the building's location, climate, and intended use when designing building envelope systems. They also highlight the role of aesthetics in envelope design and the use of prefabricated panels for efficiency and cost savings. By studying these real-world examples, we can gain a deeper understanding of the principles and considerations in building envelope design.





### Subsection: 7.2a Types of Thermal Insulation and Vapor Barriers

Thermal insulation and vapor barriers are essential components of a building's envelope. They play a crucial role in maintaining a comfortable indoor environment and reducing energy consumption. In this section, we will discuss the different types of thermal insulation and vapor barriers used in building construction.

#### 7.2a.1 Types of Thermal Insulation

Thermal insulation is a material or system that reduces the rate of heat transfer between two spaces. It is used to maintain a desired temperature within a building, whether it is to keep the interior cool in hot climates or warm in cold climates. There are several types of thermal insulation, each with its own advantages and disadvantages.

##### Fiberglass Insulation

Fiberglass insulation is one of the most commonly used types of thermal insulation. It is made from glass fibers that are spun into a mat and then compressed into batts or blankets. Fiberglass insulation is relatively inexpensive and easy to install, making it a popular choice for many building applications. However, it is not as effective as other types of insulation, and it can be a health hazard if inhaled.

##### Spray Foam Insulation

Spray foam insulation is a type of insulation that is sprayed onto the surface to be insulated. It expands and hardens, creating a tight seal that is effective in reducing heat transfer. Spray foam insulation is more expensive than fiberglass insulation, but it is also more effective and can be used in hard-to-reach areas. However, it can be messy and requires specialized equipment for installation.

##### Cellulose Insulation

Cellulose insulation is made from recycled paper and other cellulose materials. It is blown into the cavities of a building, creating a dense layer of insulation. Cellulose insulation is relatively inexpensive and effective in reducing heat transfer. However, it can be messy and requires specialized equipment for installation.

#### 7.2a.2 Types of Vapor Barriers

A vapor barrier is a material that prevents the movement of water vapor through a building's envelope. It is used to control moisture levels within a building, which is crucial for preventing mold growth and structural damage. There are two main types of vapor barriers:

##### Polyethylene Sheeting

Polyethylene sheeting is a common type of vapor barrier used in building construction. It is a thin, flexible sheet that is installed on the warm side of the insulation. Polyethylene sheeting is effective in preventing moisture transfer, but it can be damaged during construction and may need to be replaced.

##### Paint or Coating

Paint or coating can also be used as a vapor barrier. It is applied to the surface of the building, creating a barrier that prevents moisture transfer. Paint or coating is a cost-effective option, but it may not be as effective as other types of vapor barriers.

In conclusion, understanding the different types of thermal insulation and vapor barriers is crucial for designing an effective building envelope. Each type has its own advantages and disadvantages, and the choice will depend on the specific requirements of the building and the climate. 





### Subsection: 7.2b Design of Thermal Insulation and Vapor Barriers

The design of thermal insulation and vapor barriers is a crucial aspect of building construction. It involves selecting the appropriate type of insulation and barrier, as well as determining the necessary thickness and placement within the building envelope.

#### 7.2b.1 Selection of Thermal Insulation

The selection of thermal insulation depends on several factors, including the climate, building design, and budget. In hot climates, it is essential to have good thermal insulation to keep the building cool. In cold climates, thermal insulation is crucial for maintaining warmth. The building design also plays a role in the selection of insulation. For example, in a building with a flat roof, spray foam insulation may be the best option due to its ability to fill small gaps and cracks.

#### 7.2b.2 Selection of Vapor Barriers

Vapor barriers are essential in preventing moisture from entering the building and causing damage. They are typically made of plastic or other impermeable materials. The selection of a vapor barrier depends on the climate and building design. In humid climates, a vapor barrier is necessary to prevent moisture from entering the building. In dry climates, a vapor barrier may not be necessary, but it can still be beneficial in preventing moisture from entering the building.

#### 7.2b.3 Determining Thickness and Placement of Insulation and Barriers

The thickness and placement of insulation and barriers are crucial in achieving optimal performance. The thickness of insulation is determined by the R-value, which measures its resistance to heat transfer. The higher the R-value, the more effective the insulation is. The placement of insulation and barriers is also important. Insulation should be placed in areas where heat transfer is most likely to occur, such as around windows and doors. Vapor barriers should be placed on the warm side of the building envelope, typically on the inside.

#### 7.2b.4 Considerations for Sustainable Design

In addition to traditional design considerations, sustainable design also plays a role in the selection and placement of thermal insulation and vapor barriers. Sustainable design aims to minimize the environmental impact of a building while still meeting the needs of its occupants. In this context, the use of sustainable insulation materials and the placement of insulation and barriers can have a significant impact on the overall sustainability of a building.

For example, the use of recycled materials for insulation can reduce the environmental impact of the building. Additionally, the placement of insulation and barriers can also impact the overall energy efficiency of the building. By carefully considering the design of thermal insulation and vapor barriers, architects and engineers can create more sustainable buildings that meet the needs of their occupants while minimizing their impact on the environment.





### Subsection: 7.2c Case Studies

In this section, we will explore some real-world case studies that demonstrate the application of thermal insulation and vapor barriers in building construction.

#### 7.2c.1 Case Study 1: Insulation and Vapor Barrier in a Residential Building

In this case study, we will examine the application of thermal insulation and vapor barriers in a residential building located in a cold climate. The building is a single-family home with a basement, first floor, and second floor. The building envelope consists of brick veneer on the exterior and drywall on the interior.

The thermal insulation used in this building is fiberglass batt insulation, with an R-value of R-13. This type of insulation is commonly used in residential buildings due to its cost-effectiveness and ease of installation. The vapor barrier is a 6-mil polyethylene sheet, which is placed on the warm side of the building envelope, typically on the interior side.

The thickness and placement of insulation and barriers were determined based on the building design and the climate. The insulation was placed in the attic, basement, and between the floors, while the vapor barrier was placed on the interior side of the building envelope.

#### 7.2c.2 Case Study 2: Insulation and Vapor Barrier in a Commercial Building

In this case study, we will examine the application of thermal insulation and vapor barriers in a commercial building located in a hot climate. The building is a two-story office building with a flat roof. The building envelope consists of metal panels on the exterior and drywall on the interior.

The thermal insulation used in this building is spray foam insulation, with an R-value of R-7. This type of insulation is commonly used in commercial buildings due to its ability to fill small gaps and cracks, providing a more efficient barrier to heat transfer. The vapor barrier is a 6-mil polyethylene sheet, which is placed on the warm side of the building envelope, typically on the interior side.

The thickness and placement of insulation and barriers were determined based on the building design and the climate. The insulation was placed in the attic and between the floors, while the vapor barrier was placed on the interior side of the building envelope.

#### 7.2c.3 Case Study 3: Insulation and Vapor Barrier in a Green Building

In this case study, we will examine the application of thermal insulation and vapor barriers in a green building located in a temperate climate. The building is a single-family home with a basement, first floor, and second floor. The building envelope consists of straw bales on the exterior and clay plaster on the interior.

The thermal insulation used in this building is straw bales, which have an R-value of R-25. This type of insulation is commonly used in green buildings due to its natural and renewable properties. The vapor barrier is a 6-mil polyethylene sheet, which is placed on the warm side of the building envelope, typically on the interior side.

The thickness and placement of insulation and barriers were determined based on the building design and the climate. The insulation was placed in the attic, basement, and between the floors, while the vapor barrier was placed on the interior side of the building envelope.

### Conclusion

These case studies demonstrate the importance of selecting the appropriate type of insulation and barrier, as well as determining the necessary thickness and placement within the building envelope. By considering factors such as climate, building design, and budget, engineers can make informed decisions about the design of thermal insulation and vapor barriers, resulting in more efficient and sustainable buildings.





### Subsection: 7.3a Types of Waterproofing Systems

Waterproofing is a crucial aspect of building construction, particularly in areas with high moisture levels or where water infiltration can cause significant damage to the structure. There are several types of waterproofing systems, each with its own advantages and limitations. In this section, we will discuss the most common types of waterproofing systems used in building construction.

#### 7.3a.1 Bituminous Waterproofing

Bituminous waterproofing is one of the oldest and most commonly used types of waterproofing systems. It involves the application of a bituminous coating or membrane to the surface of the structure. The bitumen, which is a hydrocarbon-based substance, is mixed with various additives to improve its flexibility and durability.

Bituminous waterproofing is typically used for below-grade applications, such as basements and foundations. It is also used in areas where there is a high risk of water infiltration, such as around windows and doors. The bitumen forms a watertight seal that prevents water from entering the structure.

#### 7.3a.2 Polyurethane Waterproofing

Polyurethane waterproofing is a relatively new type of waterproofing system that has gained popularity due to its durability and flexibility. It involves the application of a polyurethane coating or membrane to the surface of the structure. The polyurethane is a synthetic polymer that is highly resistant to water and chemicals.

Polyurethane waterproofing is typically used for above-grade applications, such as roofs and balconies. It is also used in areas where there is a high risk of water infiltration, such as around windows and doors. The polyurethane forms a watertight seal that is highly resistant to punctures and tears.

#### 7.3a.3 Cementitious Waterproofing

Cementitious waterproofing is a type of waterproofing system that involves the application of a cement-based coating or membrane to the surface of the structure. The cement is mixed with various additives to improve its water resistance and durability.

Cementitious waterproofing is typically used for below-grade applications, such as basements and foundations. It is also used in areas where there is a high risk of water infiltration, such as around windows and doors. The cement forms a watertight seal that is highly resistant to water and chemicals.

#### 7.3a.4 Liquid Applied Waterproofing

Liquid applied waterproofing is a type of waterproofing system that involves the application of a liquid membrane to the surface of the structure. The liquid membrane is typically made of a polymer or a combination of polymers and additives.

Liquid applied waterproofing is typically used for below-grade applications, such as basements and foundations. It is also used in areas where there is a high risk of water infiltration, such as around windows and doors. The liquid membrane forms a watertight seal that is highly flexible and durable.

In the next section, we will discuss the design considerations for waterproofing systems.





### Subsection: 7.3b Design of Waterproofing Systems

The design of a waterproofing system is a crucial step in the construction process. It involves careful consideration of the type of waterproofing system to be used, as well as the design of the structure itself. In this section, we will discuss the key factors that must be considered when designing a waterproofing system.

#### 7.3b.1 Type of Waterproofing System

As discussed in the previous section, there are several types of waterproofing systems available. The choice of system will depend on the specific requirements of the structure, as well as the preferences of the designer and builder. For example, bituminous waterproofing may be preferred for its cost-effectiveness, while polyurethane waterproofing may be chosen for its durability and flexibility.

#### 7.3b.2 Design of the Structure

The design of the structure itself can greatly impact the effectiveness of a waterproofing system. For example, a structure with a flat roof may require a different type of waterproofing system than a structure with a pitched roof. Similarly, the design of the foundation and basement may also need to be considered.

#### 7.3b.3 Consideration of Water Infiltration Risks

It is important to consider the potential risks of water infiltration when designing a waterproofing system. This includes identifying areas of the structure that may be vulnerable to water infiltration, such as around windows and doors, and designing the waterproofing system accordingly.

#### 7.3b.4 Testing and Maintenance

As with any building system, it is important to test the waterproofing system to ensure its effectiveness. This can be done through various methods, such as hydrostatic testing or visual inspections. Additionally, regular maintenance and inspections should be scheduled to ensure the continued effectiveness of the waterproofing system.

In conclusion, the design of a waterproofing system is a crucial step in the construction process. It requires careful consideration of the type of waterproofing system, the design of the structure, and potential risks of water infiltration. By following these guidelines, a waterproofing system can be designed that effectively protects the structure from water damage.





### Subsection: 7.3c Case Studies

In this section, we will explore some real-world case studies that demonstrate the application of waterproofing systems in different types of structures. These case studies will provide valuable insights into the design and implementation of waterproofing systems, and will also highlight the importance of considering various factors such as the type of structure, potential water infiltration risks, and the effectiveness of the chosen waterproofing system.

#### 7.3c.1 Waterproofing of a Residential Building

The first case study involves the waterproofing of a residential building in a coastal area. The building has a flat roof and a basement, making it vulnerable to water infiltration. The designer chose to use a bituminous waterproofing system for its cost-effectiveness and ease of application. However, during the construction process, it was discovered that the foundation was not properly sealed, allowing water to seep into the basement. This led to a delay in the completion of the project and additional costs for waterproofing the foundation.

This case study highlights the importance of considering the design of the structure and potential water infiltration risks when choosing a waterproofing system. It also emphasizes the need for proper testing and maintenance to ensure the effectiveness of the waterproofing system.

#### 7.3c.2 Waterproofing of a Commercial Building

The second case study involves the waterproofing of a commercial building with a pitched roof. The designer chose to use a polyurethane waterproofing system for its durability and flexibility. However, during the hydrostatic testing, it was discovered that the system was not fully effective in preventing water infiltration. This led to a redesign of the waterproofing system, resulting in additional costs and delays.

This case study highlights the importance of testing and maintenance in ensuring the effectiveness of a waterproofing system. It also emphasizes the need for proper design and consideration of the structure and potential water infiltration risks.

#### 7.3c.3 Waterproofing of a Historical Building

The third case study involves the waterproofing of a historical building with a flat roof. The designer faced the challenge of preserving the historical integrity of the building while also ensuring its protection from water infiltration. The designer chose to use a combination of bituminous and polyurethane waterproofing systems, along with a drainage layer, to provide both protection and flexibility.

This case study highlights the importance of considering the historical significance of a building when choosing a waterproofing system. It also emphasizes the need for a comprehensive approach to waterproofing, taking into account various factors such as the type of structure, potential water infiltration risks, and the effectiveness of the chosen waterproofing system.

### Conclusion

These case studies demonstrate the importance of careful consideration and planning when it comes to waterproofing systems. They also highlight the need for proper testing and maintenance to ensure the effectiveness of the system. By learning from these real-world examples, designers and builders can make informed decisions when it comes to waterproofing their structures.





### Subsection: 7.4a Types of Air Barrier Systems

Air barrier systems are an essential component of building envelopes, playing a crucial role in controlling air leakage into and out of the building. These systems are designed to provide a continuous barrier to the movement of air, helping to maintain indoor air quality and energy efficiency. In this section, we will discuss the different types of air barrier systems, their components, and their importance in building design.

#### 7.4a.1 Types of Air Barrier Systems

There are several types of air barrier systems, each with its own unique characteristics and applications. These include:

- **Continuous Air Barrier Systems:** These systems are designed to provide a continuous barrier to air movement, covering the entire building envelope. They are typically made of materials with low air permeance, such as rigid foam insulation, and are installed using specialized techniques to ensure airtightness.

- **Discrete Air Barrier Systems:** These systems are used in specific areas of the building envelope, such as around windows and doors, where air leakage is a concern. They are typically made of materials with high air permeance, such as caulking or weatherstripping, and are installed using specialized techniques to ensure airtightness.

- **Hybrid Air Barrier Systems:** These systems combine the features of both continuous and discrete air barrier systems. They are typically used in complex building envelopes where both continuous and discrete barriers are required.

#### 7.4a.2 Components of Air Barrier Systems

Air barrier systems are made up of several components that work together to provide a continuous barrier to air movement. These components include:

- **Air Barrier Materials:** These are the "big" pieces of material used in an air barrier assembly. They are typically made of materials with low air permeance, such as rigid foam insulation, and are installed using specialized techniques to ensure airtightness.

- **Air Barrier Accessories:** These products are used to maintain air tightness between air barrier materials, assemblies, and components. They include sealants, tapes, backer rods, transition membranes, nails/washers, ties, clips, staples, strapping, and primers.

- **Air Barrier Components:** These are pre-manufactured elements such as windows, doors, and service elements that are installed in the environmental separator and sealed by air barrier accessories. They have an air leakage rate no greater than 0.20 L/(s‚Ä¢m¬≤) at a pressure difference of 75 Pa when tested in accordance with ASTM E 2357.

- **Air Barrier Assemblies:** These are combinations of air barrier materials and air barrier accessories that are designated and designed within the environmental separator to act as a continuous barrier to the movement of air. They have an air leakage rate no greater than 0.20 L/(s‚Ä¢m¬≤) at a pressure difference of 75 Pa when tested in accordance with ASTM E 2357.

#### 7.4a.3 Importance of Air Barrier Systems

Air barrier systems play a crucial role in building design, helping to maintain indoor air quality and energy efficiency. They are essential for controlling air leakage, which can lead to heat loss in winter and heat gain in summer, resulting in increased energy consumption and costs. Air barrier systems also help to prevent the infiltration of pollutants and allergens, improving indoor air quality and the health of building occupants.

In addition, air barrier systems are an integral part of the building envelope, working in conjunction with other systems such as insulation and vapor barriers to provide a comprehensive protection against the elements. They are also essential for meeting building codes and regulations, as many jurisdictions require the use of air barrier systems to ensure the energy efficiency and durability of buildings.

In conclusion, air barrier systems are a crucial component of building envelopes, providing a continuous barrier to air movement and helping to maintain indoor air quality and energy efficiency. Understanding the different types of air barrier systems, their components, and their importance in building design is essential for any building professional.





### Subsection: 7.4b Design of Air Barrier Systems

The design of air barrier systems is a crucial step in building construction. It involves careful consideration of the building's design, materials, and construction techniques to ensure the effectiveness of the air barrier. In this section, we will discuss the design considerations for air barrier systems.

#### 7.4b.1 Design Considerations for Air Barrier Systems

When designing an air barrier system, several factors must be considered to ensure its effectiveness. These include:

- **Building Design:** The design of the building can greatly impact the effectiveness of the air barrier system. For example, a building with a complex geometry or multiple levels may require a hybrid air barrier system to address both continuous and discrete areas.

- **Material Selection:** The choice of materials for the air barrier system is crucial. Materials with low air permeance, such as rigid foam insulation, are typically used for continuous air barrier systems. Discrete air barrier systems may use materials with high air permeance, such as caulking or weatherstripping.

- **Construction Techniques:** The installation of the air barrier system is just as important as the materials used. Specialized techniques, such as sealing joints and seams, must be used to ensure airtightness.

- **Testing and Verification:** Finally, it is essential to test and verify the effectiveness of the air barrier system. This can be done through field testing or laboratory testing, and should be done before the building is occupied to ensure its effectiveness.

#### 7.4b.2 Design Tools for Air Barrier Systems

To aid in the design of air barrier systems, several tools and standards have been developed. These include:

- **ASHRAE Standard 90.2:** This standard provides guidelines for the design of energy-efficient buildings, including recommendations for air barrier systems.

- **ISO 12006:** This international standard provides guidelines for the design and construction of building envelopes, including air barrier systems.

- **WUFI:** This software tool, developed by the Fraunhofer Institute for Building Physics, is used to simulate the thermal and moisture behavior of building envelopes, including air barrier systems.

By considering these design considerations and utilizing these tools, architects and engineers can design effective air barrier systems that contribute to the overall energy efficiency and indoor air quality of buildings.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the various aspects of building envelopes, focusing on the design and construction of air barrier systems. We have discussed the importance of air barriers in maintaining indoor air quality, energy efficiency, and occupant comfort. We have also examined the different types of air barrier systems, their components, and the design considerations that must be taken into account.

The design of air barrier systems is a complex process that requires careful consideration of various factors, including the building's geometry, the materials used, and the construction techniques employed. It is crucial to ensure that the air barrier system is continuous and airtight, with no gaps or weak points that could compromise its effectiveness.

In conclusion, the design and construction of air barrier systems are integral parts of building technologies. They play a crucial role in creating a healthy and comfortable indoor environment, and their importance cannot be overstated. As we continue to advance in the field of building technologies, it is essential to keep up with the latest developments and techniques in the design and construction of air barrier systems.

#### Exercise 2

## Chapter: Chapter 8: Openings:

### Introduction

Welcome to Chapter 8 of "Building Technologies III: Building Structural Systems II". This chapter is dedicated to the exploration of openings in building structures. Openings, as the name suggests, are the spaces or gaps in a building's structure that allow for the passage of light, air, and other elements. They are an integral part of any building, contributing to its functionality, aesthetics, and energy efficiency.

In this chapter, we will delve into the various aspects of openings, starting with their definition and importance. We will then explore the different types of openings, such as windows, doors, and vents, and discuss their unique characteristics and functions. We will also examine the principles and techniques used in the design and construction of openings, including the use of advanced technologies and materials.

Furthermore, we will discuss the role of openings in energy conservation and the impact of their design on a building's energy performance. We will also touch upon the concept of daylighting and its benefits, as well as the challenges and solutions associated with incorporating daylighting into building design.

Finally, we will look at the future trends in opening design and technology, and how these advancements are shaping the future of building construction. By the end of this chapter, you will have a comprehensive understanding of openings and their role in building structures, and be equipped with the knowledge to design and construct openings that meet the specific needs and requirements of any building.




#### 7.4c Case Studies

##### Case Study 1: The BTR-4 Armored Personnel Carrier

The BTR-4 is a modern armored personnel carrier used by various military forces around the world. The design of the BTR-4 includes an air barrier system to protect the occupants from environmental conditions and noise. The air barrier system is designed using a combination of continuous and discrete air barrier systems, with rigid foam insulation used for continuous areas and caulking used for discrete areas. The effectiveness of the air barrier system is tested and verified through field testing before deployment.

##### Case Study 2: The Factory Automation Infrastructure Project

The Factory Automation Infrastructure Project is a research project aimed at developing advanced automation systems for industrial applications. The project includes the development of an air barrier system for a test facility, with a focus on minimizing energy losses and controlling temperature and humidity levels. The air barrier system is designed using a hybrid approach, with rigid foam insulation used for continuous areas and caulking used for discrete areas. The effectiveness of the air barrier system is tested and verified through laboratory testing.

##### Case Study 3: The Bcache Project

The Bcache project is a research project aimed at developing a cache system for building data. The project includes the development of an air barrier system for a data center, with a focus on minimizing energy losses and controlling temperature and humidity levels. The air barrier system is designed using a combination of continuous and discrete air barrier systems, with rigid foam insulation used for continuous areas and caulking used for discrete areas. The effectiveness of the air barrier system is tested and verified through field testing.

##### Case Study 4: The GUSE Project

The GUSE project is a research project aimed at developing a workflow development infrastructure for building data. The project includes the development of an air barrier system for a research facility, with a focus on minimizing energy losses and controlling temperature and humidity levels. The air barrier system is designed using a combination of continuous and discrete air barrier systems, with rigid foam insulation used for continuous areas and caulking used for discrete areas. The effectiveness of the air barrier system is tested and verified through laboratory testing.

##### Case Study 5: The Vulcan FlipStart Project

The Vulcan FlipStart project is a research project aimed at developing a portable computer for mobile applications. The project includes the development of an air barrier system for the computer, with a focus on minimizing energy losses and controlling temperature and humidity levels. The air barrier system is designed using a combination of continuous and discrete air barrier systems, with rigid foam insulation used for continuous areas and caulking used for discrete areas. The effectiveness of the air barrier system is tested and verified through laboratory testing.




### Section: 7.5 Envelope Design Principles:

The design of a building's envelope is a critical aspect of its construction, as it serves as the first line of defense against the elements. The envelope is responsible for maintaining a comfortable interior environment, controlling energy losses, and protecting the structural integrity of the building. In this section, we will discuss the principles of envelope design, including the concept of airtightness and the role of air barrier systems.

#### 7.5a Basic Envelope Design Principles

The design of a building's envelope is governed by a set of principles that aim to achieve a balance between functionality, durability, and energy efficiency. These principles include:

1. Airtightness: The envelope should be designed to minimize air infiltration and exfiltration, which can lead to energy losses and discomfort for occupants. This is achieved through the use of air barrier systems, which are discussed in more detail in the previous section.

2. Thermal resistance: The envelope should provide adequate insulation to control heat transfer and maintain a comfortable interior temperature. This is achieved through the use of insulation materials, such as rigid foam or fiberglass, and proper detailing of the envelope.

3. Moisture control: The envelope should be designed to manage moisture effectively, preventing condensation and mold growth. This is achieved through the use of vapor barriers and proper detailing of the envelope.

4. Durability: The envelope should be designed to withstand the effects of weather and other environmental factors, ensuring the long-term integrity of the building. This is achieved through the use of durable materials and proper detailing of the envelope.

5. Sustainability: The envelope should be designed with sustainability in mind, considering the environmental impact of its materials and construction. This can be achieved through the use of recycled or renewable materials, and through the implementation of energy-efficient design strategies.

#### 7.5b Envelope Design Strategies

In addition to the principles of envelope design, there are several strategies that can be employed to achieve a high-performance envelope. These strategies include:

1. Passive design: Passive design strategies aim to minimize the need for active heating and cooling systems by taking advantage of natural resources, such as sunlight and ventilation. This can be achieved through the use of south-facing windows, shading devices, and cross-ventilation.

2. Active design: Active design strategies involve the use of mechanical systems, such as HVAC systems, to control the interior environment. This can be achieved through the use of heat recovery ventilation (HRV) systems, which recover heat from exhaust air, and demand-controlled ventilation (DCV) systems, which adjust ventilation rates based on occupancy levels.

3. Integrated design: Integrated design involves the consideration of the envelope in conjunction with other building systems, such as the structure and mechanical systems. This can lead to more efficient and effective design solutions, as the envelope can be optimized to work in conjunction with other systems.

4. Performance-based design: Performance-based design involves setting specific performance criteria for the envelope, such as airtightness or thermal resistance, and designing the envelope to meet these criteria. This can lead to more innovative and efficient design solutions, as designers are not limited by traditional design conventions.

#### 7.5c Case Studies

To further illustrate these principles and strategies, let's examine some case studies of envelope design.

##### Case Study 1: The Bullitt Center

The Bullitt Center, located in Seattle, Washington, is often referred to as the "greenest commercial building in the world." Its envelope design is a prime example of integrated design and performance-based design. The envelope is designed to be airtight, with a blower door test result of 0.25 ACH50, and is also designed to provide excellent thermal resistance. The envelope is composed of a timber frame structure, with a rainscreen cladding system and triple-pane glazing. The building also employs active design strategies, with an HRV system and DCV system.

##### Case Study 2: The Crystal

The Crystal, located in London, England, is a sustainable building that serves as a conference center and exhibition space. Its envelope design is a prime example of passive design. The building is oriented to take advantage of natural sunlight, with south-facing windows and shading devices. The envelope also employs cross-ventilation strategies, with operable windows on all sides of the building. The building also employs active design strategies, with an HRV system and DCV system.

##### Case Study 3: The BTR-4 Armored Personnel Carrier

The BTR-4, a modern armored personnel carrier, employs a hybrid envelope design. The envelope is composed of a steel frame, with composite armor panels on the exterior. The envelope is designed to be airtight, with a blower door test result of 0.5 ACH50. The envelope also employs passive design strategies, with south-facing windows and shading devices. The building also employs active design strategies, with an HRV system and DCV system.

#### 7.5d Conclusion

In conclusion, the design of a building's envelope is a complex process that requires careful consideration of a variety of principles and strategies. By employing these principles and strategies, designers can create high-performance envelopes that provide a comfortable and sustainable interior environment for building occupants.




### Subsection: 7.5b Design for Envelope Durability

The durability of a building's envelope is a critical aspect of its long-term performance. It is essential to consider durability during the design phase to ensure that the envelope can withstand the effects of weather, aging, and other environmental factors. In this subsection, we will discuss the principles of designing for envelope durability.

#### 7.5b.1 Material Selection

The choice of materials for the envelope plays a significant role in its durability. The materials should be able to withstand the environmental conditions they will be exposed to, such as extreme temperatures, UV radiation, and moisture. For example, in areas with high UV radiation, materials with good UV resistance should be used. Similarly, in areas with high moisture levels, materials with good moisture resistance should be chosen.

#### 7.5b.2 Detailing and Construction

The detailing and construction of the envelope also contribute to its durability. Proper detailing, such as flashing and caulking, can help prevent water infiltration and damage to the envelope. The construction process should also be carefully managed to avoid defects that can compromise the durability of the envelope.

#### 7.5b.3 Maintenance and Repair

Regular maintenance and repair are essential for maintaining the durability of the envelope. This includes inspecting the envelope for signs of damage, such as cracks or leaks, and making necessary repairs. Regular maintenance can help identify and address issues early, preventing more significant damage to the envelope.

#### 7.5b.4 Envelope System Integration

The envelope should be integrated with other building systems, such as the roof and foundation, to ensure its durability. For example, the envelope should be designed to work in conjunction with the roof to prevent water infiltration. Similarly, the envelope should be designed to work with the foundation to prevent moisture infiltration from the ground.

In conclusion, designing for envelope durability involves careful consideration of material selection, detailing and construction, maintenance and repair, and system integration. By following these principles, the envelope can be designed to withstand the effects of weather and other environmental factors, ensuring the long-term integrity of the building.





### Subsection: 7.5c Design for Envelope Aesthetics

The aesthetic appeal of a building's envelope is an important aspect of its design. It not only adds to the overall visual appeal of the building but also contributes to its marketability and resale value. In this subsection, we will discuss the principles of designing for envelope aesthetics.

#### 7.5c.1 Material Selection

The choice of materials for the envelope can greatly impact its aesthetic appeal. The materials should not only be functional but also visually appealing. For example, the use of natural materials such as wood or stone can add a sense of warmth and elegance to the building. Similarly, the use of colorful materials can add a pop of color and vibrancy to the building.

#### 7.5c.2 Detailing and Construction

The detailing and construction of the envelope can also contribute to its aesthetic appeal. Proper detailing, such as the use of decorative elements or intricate patterns, can add visual interest to the envelope. The construction process should also be carefully managed to ensure that the aesthetic intent of the design is maintained.

#### 7.5c.3 Maintenance and Repair

Regular maintenance and repair are not only essential for the durability of the envelope but also for its aesthetic appeal. Damage to the envelope can detract from its visual appeal and should be addressed promptly to maintain the building's aesthetic appeal.

#### 7.5c.4 Envelope System Integration

The envelope should be integrated with other building systems, such as the roof and foundation, to ensure its aesthetic appeal. For example, the use of matching materials or colors can create a sense of unity and cohesiveness in the building's design. Similarly, the integration of the envelope with the surrounding landscape can add to the overall aesthetic appeal of the building.




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the various components of building envelopes and their importance in the overall structural system of a building. We have discussed the different types of envelopes, including the building skin, roof, and foundation, and how they work together to protect the building from external forces such as wind, water, and temperature changes. We have also delved into the design considerations for each type of envelope, including material selection, energy efficiency, and durability.

One key takeaway from this chapter is the importance of considering the building envelope as a whole, rather than just individual components. The building envelope is a complex system that must work together to provide a safe and efficient structure. Therefore, it is crucial for architects and engineers to carefully consider the interactions between the different envelope components and how they will affect the overall performance of the building.

Another important aspect to consider is the impact of the building envelope on the overall energy efficiency of a building. As we have discussed, the building envelope plays a significant role in regulating the flow of heat, light, and air into and out of a building. By carefully designing and selecting materials for the building envelope, we can greatly improve the energy efficiency of a building, reducing heating and cooling costs and promoting sustainability.

In conclusion, the building envelope is a crucial component of any building, and its design and construction must be carefully considered to ensure the safety, durability, and energy efficiency of the structure. By understanding the different types of envelopes and their design considerations, architects and engineers can create more efficient and sustainable buildings for the future.

As we have discussed, the building envelope plays a significant role in regulating the flow of heat, light, and air into and out of a building. By carefully designing and selecting materials for the building envelope, we can greatly improve the energy efficiency of a building, reducing heating and cooling costs and promoting sustainability.

In conclusion, the building envelope is a crucial component of any building, and its design and construction must be carefully considered to ensure the safety, durability, and energy efficiency of the structure. By understanding the different types of envelopes and their design considerations, architects and engineers can create more efficient and sustainable buildings for the future.

Each of these systems plays a unique role in supporting the weight of the building and distributing it evenly. We will also explore the advantages and disadvantages of each system and how they are used in different types of buildings.

Next, we will delve into the design considerations for structural systems. This includes factors such as load capacity, structural integrity, and cost. We will also discuss the importance of considering the surrounding environment and how it can impact the design of a structural system.

These methods have revolutionized the way buildings are constructed and have become increasingly popular in recent years. This knowledge will be invaluable in your journey to becoming a successful architect or engineer. So let's dive in and explore the world of building structural systems.


## Chapter 8: Structural Systems:

In the ever-evolving field of building technology, advancements are constantly being made to improve the efficiency, safety, and sustainability of structures.
